Northeast Customs and Postal Issues 106

Related to the Entire Northeast, Not a Simple Issue

The Government Formulates Concrete Plans in Preparation for Negotiations

Guo Taiqi Speaks: A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Minister Guo Taiqi at his residence yesterday to inquire about his views on the puppet state's seizure of customs duties and postal rights in the Northeast. According to Guo, the puppet state's attempt to seize customs duties and postal rights in the Northeast is not a simple issue. Japan's presence in the Northeast began with instructing a small number of puppets to organize the so-called "Government of Manchuria," with Japanese advisors and consultants holding real power. Then, it openly recognized the puppet state, not hesitating to tear off its last mask, and finally seized customs duties and postal rights in the Northeast, undermining the integrity of China's administration. The so-called "Government of Manchuria" is merely a puppet organization, and Japan cannot shirk its responsibility for all its words and deeds. On the one hand, Japan signed a ceasefire agreement with us in Shanghai, hoping that the friendship between the two countries and the feelings of the two peoples would gradually recover. On the other hand, it acted arbitrarily in the Northeast. This contradictory behavior must be due to an error in the observation of the Japanese authorities or a contempt for our country. The three northeastern provinces are Chinese territory. The puppet state's attempt to seize customs duties and postal rights in the three provinces is by no means as simple as it appears on the surface. This is the entire issue of the Northeast, and it is the entire issue of China. How can it be merely a simple issue of customs duties and postal rights? It is hoped that the people and the government will cooperate effectively and actively recover the Northeast to protect the integrity of our country's land and administration, Guo said. After Guo finished speaking, the reporter asked about his date of going to Beijing. Guo said that he would go to Beijing in two or three days because there are still several matters that need to be discussed with President Wang and Minister Luo, as well as to say goodbye to Wang Luo and relatives and friends in Beijing. After staying in Beijing for a few days, he will return to Shanghai to pack up and prepare to go to England to take office at the beginning of next month.

Huang Naishu Speaks: A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Huang Naishu, the director of the Postal Administration, yesterday to inquire about his views on the Northeast postal issue and the measures to be taken. He received a very detailed answer. Huang said that the three northeastern provinces are divided into two postal districts: the Liaoning District and the Jilin-Heilongjiang District, with annual revenue of approximately 2 million yuan. Since the September 18th Incident, the puppet organization has been eager to seize it, but it has not yet succeeded. Recent reports indicate that the puppet state has decided to send personnel to forcibly seize it starting on July 1st and has already begun printing fake stamps, seemingly determined to achieve its seizure goal. However, the postal service is an integral part of the country's overall business and cannot be abandoned under any circumstances. If the puppet state really wants to send personnel to forcibly take over, then the postal organizations in the three provinces will have to be abolished uniformly, and all staff will be recalled uniformly. He also said that the postal revenue of the three northeastern provinces is very large. If it is seized, the annual revenue will be reduced, and the impact on the postal service itself will be significant. Currently, the government has formulated concrete plans in preparation for negotiations.

The Municipal Government Announces Tax Reductions and Exemptions in the War Zone 107

Municipal Revenue Reduced by One Million Yuan

Since the Shanghai war, the masses in the war zone have been displaced, and their property and assets have been mostly lost. They are unable to recover at this time, and the future is dire. The victims after the disaster are looking to the government for assistance. If wartime taxes are still collected, it would not reflect the intention of caring for the people's hardships. Therefore, Mayor Wu convened the relevant bureaus to discuss the reduction and exemption of various taxes in the war zone. The final decision was announced to the public yesterday.

Municipal Government Announcement: Regarding the announcement, it is found that this city has suffered greatly from the war. All the people in the war zone have suffered great losses due to the sudden occurrence of the incident. They have been displaced and have endured great suffering. The municipal government is deeply saddened and sympathizes deeply. The policy of caring for the people in ancient times relies on tangible benefits for the people. Reducing taxes is a top priority. Therefore, the municipal government has carefully considered the situation of the house tax and various taxes in the war zone and has formulated various reduction and exemption measures to slightly lighten the burden on the disaster victims, so that they can spare their strength to engage in the recovery of their businesses. Then, the harvest in the sunset is still not too late. Now, the municipal government has specially recorded the tax reduction and exemption measures in the war zone and announced them to the public. This announcement,

Reduction and Exemption Measures: 1. House tax: fully exempt for the spring and summer seasons in the war zone. 2. Business rickshaws: excluding those that have been moved to the southern taxation office to pay taxes and operate, the tax collection for vehicles in the remaining war zones will begin in June. Public buses of Shanghai-Taicang Company and Chinese-owned companies will be taxed from the month of resumption of operation. 3. Advertising tax: exempt for two seasons. 4. Ferry tax: to be taxed from the month of resumption of ferry service. 5. Amusement tax: to be taxed from the date of resumption of business. 6. Stall tax: to be taxed from the month of resumption of stalls. 7. Vegetable market tax: to be taxed from the month of resumption of business. 8. Teahouse tax: to be taxed from the month of resumption of business. 9. Reduction and exemption of land tax: because it is related to the area under the jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province, it should be determined after consultation. At the same time, the precedents for disaster relief and tax exemption should be followed, starting with investigation, distinguishing between severity, and jointly deciding by the relevant bureaus. 10. The two first and second civilian residences and the slaughterhouse buildings in Zhabei will be exempt from three months' rent for the second, third, and fourth classes. 11. The rent of the Wusong public property will be examined and verified after officials from the northern taxation office are instructed to investigate the situation.

Loss of Municipal Revenue: After the implementation of the above various tax reduction and exemption measures by the municipal government bureaus, according to Secretary-General Yu, the total loss is estimated to be over one million. However, municipal administration aspects such as sanitation and construction will continue to be actively carried out and will not be hindered by the reduction in revenue.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Exemption from National Taxes in the Songhu Area 108

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating: "The attached is a request for the matter. The association held its third membership meeting on June 18th. According to the proposals of members Ye Jiaxing, Mao Chunpu, Ling Zhijia, Zhu Binglu, Fei Tinghua, and Chen Wenming, and seconded by Jin Chuxiang, Qiu Liangyu, Jin Wenxiang, Lu Fusheng, Gu Jixiang, and Gu Hongxiang, to request the government to exempt the national and local taxes in the Songhu disaster area to facilitate recovery, the members' meeting on that day resolved to request the government to exempt the taxes. It has been the practice in our country to exempt the areas occupied and disturbed by robbers from paying inland grain and corvée for a certain period of time after the matter is settled. This can be traced back to the pre-Qing Dynasty. This year, the Japanese army occupied Songhu, and the devastation from the city to the countryside has been unprecedented in a century, which is in line with the precedent for exempting inland grain and corvée. In the past, the tax items were simple. In addition to inland grain and corvée, the country had no other sources of revenue. Now, the tax items have become more extensive, and the precedent for exemption should be extended to general national and local taxes, so that the war zone can be slightly relieved and the resumption of business can be hoped for. It is reasonable to record the case and request the approval of your Yuan, and to instruct the Ministry of Finance and the Shanghai Municipal Government to separately exempt them, which would be for the public good."

The Japanese Army in District D to Withdraw in the Shortest Possible Time 109

Results of Yesterday's Discussion by the Joint Committee

The Japanese Army at Gongda and Other Places May Also Withdraw Soon

The Joint Committee held a meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday with representatives from both China and Japan to discuss the withdrawal of troops from District D. After one hour and thirty minutes of debate, the Japanese side agreed to completely withdraw the more than 3,000 Japanese Marine Corps troops in the area in the shortest possible time. The details of the discussion are as follows:

Questions Raised: Yesterday morning, the Chinese and Japanese representatives agreed in advance to meet at the American Consulate on Jiujiang Road at 10:00 AM. At that time, Chinese representative Yu Hongjun and Japanese representatives Okazaki and Yajima arrived on time. Regarding the content of the discussion, Mr. Yu first raised a question to the Japanese representative, saying that the Japanese army in District D had been repeatedly delayed and had not yet made a definite statement on withdrawal. The citizens of the city are quite skeptical and critical. I wonder when your side can actually implement the withdrawal. Please give a definite reply to strengthen friendship. At this point, the Japanese representative Okazaki stood up and replied, "District D was originally designated as a temporary stationing area for the Japanese army in the ceasefire agreement, so the Japanese army still needs to extend the time and may not be able to withdraw immediately."

Finally Agreed to Withdraw: Mr. Yu then refuted this by citing two points: According to the provisions of the ceasefire agreement, the temporary stationing area was designated for the Japanese army because it was not able to withdraw completely at once. Therefore, this area was designated as a temporary stationing area for the Japanese army. Now that the Japanese army has all returned home, this area should be completely returned to China for takeover within four weeks. (2) According to the agreement, the status quo before January 28th must be restored within four weeks. Therefore, the withdrawal of the Japanese army is very clear. The Japanese army has been overdue for a long time and has not withdrawn. The Chinese side sincerely believed that the withdrawal of the Japanese army may require some preparation in fact, so it did not urge it very much, waiting for your side to maintain its credibility and give a scheduled notice. Now that we have waited for a long time, we hope that your side will completely withdraw the troops in District D as soon as possible to fulfill the agreement and respect sovereignty. Then the Japanese representative pondered for a while and changed his tone and said, "After the troops have made some preparations, they will withdraw as soon as possible." The debate ended at 11:30 AM and the meeting was adjourned.

Also Withdrawing from Four Other Places: Regarding the Japanese army at Gongda Yarn Factory, Tongwen College, Rihua Yarn Factory, and Toyota Yarn Factory, the Japanese side had long agreed to withdraw within the day, but it has not yet been implemented as of yesterday, leading to the speculation that the Japanese army at the four places is still a problem. At the same time, the Japanese side countered the propaganda, saying that the Japanese army at the four places would never withdraw (see Shanghai Daily News). However, according to Yu Hongjun of the Joint Committee, the Japanese side has agreed to withdraw the Japanese army at the four places, which will of course be withdrawn and is not a problem. In addition, the request of Japanese residents to organize a patrol team has been investigated and is not a fact.

Songhu Committee Submits Document: Tang Chengzong and Liu Ziwen, members of the Wusong Municipal Committee, submitted a document to Mayor Wu yesterday, stating: "The attached is a request for negotiations to withdraw the Japanese army from the occupied area as soon as possible in order to stabilize the people's hearts and benefit the recovery. Since the completion of the agreement, the Wusong area has been taken over by us, and the people have gradually moved back and built houses to live in. It is estimated that 90% of the rural areas have been occupied, while only 30% of the town area has been occupied. The reason for this is that the Huafeng Yarn Factory in the west of the town still has dozens of Japanese Marine Corps troops stationed there. The people have been like startled birds after this catastrophe, and the location of the Japanese Marine Corps is close at hand. No wonder the people are hesitant to move forward. Moreover, unemployed vagrants deliberately spread rumors to create chaos, and ignorant people are even more panicked. The committee members have heard and seen this and cannot remain silent. Therefore, they have prepared a document and requested the mayor to seriously negotiate to ensure that the Japanese Marine Corps stationed in the Huafeng Yarn Factory is withdrawn as soon as possible in order to stabilize the people's hearts and benefit the recovery."

Armory Shutdown 112

Song Ren is Scheduled to Complete Closure by the End of This Month

The Guowen News Agency reports that the Shanghai Armory has received an order from the Ministry of Military Administration to cease operations. The handling committee has ordered that the existing armory machinery be distributed to the Jinling, Hanyang, and Gongxian armories. Currently, Song Ren's mission is scheduled to be completed by the end of this month. Future disposition matters will be the responsibility of the handling committee. Regarding the reasons for the shutdown, our reporter has learned the following summary:

Process of Shutdown The factory was originally transformed from a Western-owned shipbuilding factory in Hongkou, purchased during the Qing Dynasty under Li Hongzhang. It underwent several expansions and was moved to Gaochang Temple, totaling fifty to sixty years of operation. During the recent Shanghai battle, workers were dismissed, leaving only the artillery factory to continue working. Two weeks before the war subsided, the labor union, for the sake of maintaining operations, sent representatives twice to the Beijing Military Affairs Committee, Ministry of Military Administration, and Armory Department to request resumption of work. It is said that when the representatives met Chairman Chiang at the Military Affairs Committee, Chiang stated that the matter fell under the scope of military administration and instructed them to seek solutions from the Ministry of Military Administration. The Ministry informed them that work could resume within three weeks, and that funding from superiors had been approved at 80,000 yuan per month, resulting in a very satisfactory outcome. Unexpectedly, last month, the Ministry sent Western consultant Bloomai to Shanghai to inspect the factory. After assessing the situation of the war, Bloomai reported that it was not appropriate to establish armory facilities near commercial ports. Furthermore, there were proposals in Shanghai in the fourteenth year of the Republic to relocate. Therefore, he submitted a detailed proposal to the Military Affairs Committee. The committee discussed and agreed that the proposal was accurate. Chairman Chiang approved the proposal, leading to the shutdown and merger of the factory.

Post-Shutdown Handling The post-shutdown handling committee of the factory has already convened in Beijing. However, the committee member list differs slightly from yesterday's report. The committee is set at eight members, including the directors of the Jinling Armory, Li Chenggan, the Hanyang Armory, Huang Gongzhu, and the Shanghai Armory, Song Ren. Additionally, one person will be nominated from the materials committee of the Armory Department, and the heads of the design, general affairs, audit, and supervision sections of the Armory Department will jointly handle the matter.

Current Situation Before the war, the factory had over 4,000 employees. Due to the war, many workers were dismissed. Currently, there are fewer than 400 employees. Investigations reveal that the current artillery factory has over 180 workers. The gun factory, bullet factory, shell factory, medicine factory, and machinery factory each have twelve workers. Various department staff number over sixty, and the remaining security team consists of one squad of over thirty, totaling three hundred forty to fifty people.

Labor Union's Intentions Yesterday, the Guowen News Agency reporter inquired with the labor union about their intentions. The workers stated that the results of their petition in Beijing the previous week were very positive, making the current situation unexpected. The labor union plans to continue petitioning the government based on three reasons: (1) Moving the Shanghai factory's machinery to Jinling, Hanyang, and Gongxian would require new factory buildings, which is unnecessary. (2) Moving machinery from Hangzhou back to Shanghai is closer and more convenient. (3) Abandoning the existing machine foundations and building new ones would be very costly. However, the government is already taking concrete actions, making it difficult to reverse the decision. The factory previously sent Hu Sihong, head of the inspection department, and two others to Beijing to explain the historical situation, not to request a reversal of the decision.

Orders Not Received A Datong News Agency reporter visited the armory yesterday to interview Director Song Ren. Song sent Zhang Bochou, the head of the document section, to represent him. According to Zhang, the orders from the Ministry of Military Administration and the Armory Department regarding whether the factory would shut down have not yet arrived. Until the orders are received, work will continue as usual to maintain the status quo. Regarding the mission of Hu Sihong, head of the inspection department, and others to Beijing, Zhang stated that he was not aware of it.

Party Support The armory has attached branches of the Chinese Nationalist Party Shanghai District 25, 28, 30, and 31. Most of the party members are workers at the factory. Since receiving news of the factory shutdown, they have gathered to discuss and petition the upper-level party organization to forward the matter to the Central Government, requesting the military department to withdraw the previous proposal and restore work.

End of Labor Strike at the Concession Telephone Company 113

Strike Committee Resolved Yesterday

Painfully Resuming Work Today

After the labor strike at the Concession Telephone Company, the strike committee, due to a portion of workers resuming work without authorization and facing adverse conditions, ordered all workers to painfully resume work starting today. They also issued a declaration preparing for a second struggle. Details are as follows:

Increased Resumption Since a small number of workers at the Xinzhongyang Branch on Fujian Road, the Fanan Branch on Bixun Road, and the Beihang Branch on Haining Road resumed work the day before yesterday, the engineers of the company, including Wilson, contacted various workers and persuaded them to return to work. At the same time, the police department dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to station at various branches to protect those resuming work and to drive away the liaison office of the strike committee at No. 85, Avenue Edward VII, preventing workers and the strike committee from communicating. From yesterday onwards, workers from the Jiangxi Road Headquarters, Fujian Road, Haining Road, Huishan Road, Matt Hess Road, Yangshupu, Bixun Road, Yidingpan Road, and Trinity Yin Road branches have successively returned to work, accounting for seven-tenths of the total workforce.

Meeting Prohibited The strike committee originally planned to gather at 10:00 AM yesterday at No. 513, Far East Hotel, to hold an emergency meeting to discuss whether to continue the strike and adopt effective measures to deal with the company. However, at 8:30 AM, the Public Concession Police Department dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to prevent the meeting and drive away the striking workers. They also notified the accounting department of the Far East Hotel to prohibit renting the premises to telephone workers as an office. As a result, the striking workers withdrew from the temporary meeting of the strike committee and continued to hold discussions on the roadside in front of the Far East Hotel, but were again prevented by the police department, making it impossible to hold a mass meeting.

Emergency Meeting In view of the fact that the mass meeting was prevented by the police department, the strike committee held an emergency meeting at a teahouse on Fujian Road at 11:00 AM. More than 100 striking workers from Jiangxi Road and Fujian Road attended. The chairman first reported on the current situation and the strike trend, noting that the environment was very harsh. They then began discussions. The striking workers believed that the foremen had deceived and pressured workers to return to work, and advocated using force to deal with the company and destructive measures. They supported the strike committee in continuing the strike. The strike committee, seeing that a large portion of the workers had already resumed work without authorization and that the strike trend had tragically failed, advised them to painfully resume work. The following resolutions were made on the spot: (1) Painfully resume work; (2) Issue a declaration; (3) Prepare for a second struggle. Finally, they dispersed after shouting slogans.

Strike Committee Order The strike committee issued an order stating: "Fellow workers, our strike this time has been undermined by the sabotage of traitors and running dogs, the oppression of the imperialist police department, and the lack of internal solidarity among the workers. We have failed to attract a majority of workers to work under the strike committee. As a result, today's strike cannot be sustained. Therefore, we have no choice but to painfully resume work and preserve our strength to prepare for the next more determined strike. We hope that all workers will resume work in an organized manner this afternoon and tomorrow morning, strengthen our own organization, resist the attacks of the capitalists, and prepare to fight for the next victory. This notice is issued by the Shanghai Telephone Company Employees' Strike Committee on June 21."

Declaration of Resumption To all Shanghai workers and people from all walks of life, we, the more than three thousand telephone workers, have been on strike against the American imperialist capitalists for thirteen days in pursuit of our own interests. However, due to the oppression of the imperialist police department, the prohibition of our meetings, the surveillance of our organization, the arrest of our fellow workers, the sabotage of traitors and running dogs, the deception and intimidation of workers by foremen to return to work, and the undermining of worker solidarity, as well as the unsound internal organization of the workers, the lack of solidarity, the failure of the strike committee to include representatives of workers from all departments, the lack of close relationship with the masses, and the failure to mobilize the majority of workers to participate in the work of the strike committee, we have not been able to organize the masses in a timely manner to attack the enemy. Therefore, although we have expelled from the strike committee those wavering, compromising, advocating unconditional resumption of work, and requesting official and party "arbitration and mediation" corrupt elements that undermine the strike, we have still failed to launch a broader mass of positive action to achieve the victory of the strike. Under the oppression of the imperial authorities and the sabotage of traitors and running dogs, this strike has failed. Although we have not achieved a conditional victory, our three thousand workers' heroic struggle has given the American imperialist capitalists a great and meaningful blow. During the strike, we have learned many experiences and lessons. We have recognized that foremen and others are helping the capitalists to undermine our strike. We can only achieve our victory by establishing a strong strike committee that includes representatives of active workers from all departments, resolutely launching positive actions by the masses, eliminating traitors and running dogs, and persistently attacking the capitalists. Although we have returned to work, the conditions have not been met. At the same time, the capitalists and all traitors and running dogs will inevitably launch even tighter attacks against us, firing our workers. Therefore, although our struggle has not yielded results, we must continue to fight for our conditions. We cannot abandon the weapons of struggle in the slightest. We must continue to unite our strength, use the lessons of this strike to correct our mistakes and shortcomings, and prepare for the next more determined and greater struggle and strike. Failure is the mother of success. We will not be discouraged or passive. We will continue to unite with all Shanghai workers and the people to fight for our common victory and against our common enemy. We are very grateful to all sectors for their assistance in this strike. But we still hope that all sectors will continue to assist us. We will always stand with all Shanghai workers to oppose imperialist capitalists. Our final slogans are: (1) Down with the traitors and running dogs who undermine the strike! (2) Prepare for the next strike! (3) Oppose the capitalists' attacks on us, oppose firing workers, demand increased wages, restore Sunday work, and pay wages for the strike period. Consolidate our unity and organize our own telephone workers' union. (4) All Shanghai workers unite! (5) Down with the imperialist capitalists! Telephone Workers' Strike Committee, June 21.

Company Notice The Shanghai Telephone Company issued a notice yesterday stating that a majority of workers have now resumed work. The company has sufficient staff to maintain operations. The company is now giving the remaining personnel until June 23 to resume work. Otherwise, they will be replaced or dismissed. The wages of those who have not resumed work will be cancelled after June 23. The workers who damaged the equipment have already been fired.

Han Guojun and Others Request Allocation of Grand Canal Construction Funds 115

Han Guojun, Ma Shijie, and Others Send a Telegram:

Mr. Liangcai, transferred to Director Xi, Construction and Relief Office of the National Government Relief Committee,

Last year, the Grand Canal's dikes collapsed in over twenty locations, large and small, spanning nine hundred zhang. The estimated construction cost was four million five hundred thousand yuan. Due to difficulties in raising funds, it was reduced to three million two hundred thousand yuan. Additionally, twenty-four thousand yuan was added for crushed stone on the west dike, totaling three million four hundred and forty thousand yuan, already the bare minimum. Repairing the breached dikes is extremely difficult. In the past, the repair of just one breach at Qingshuitan cost several million taels. Every time the Yellow River breaches, it requires no less than several million yuan. There are clear precedents for this. The ten counties east of the Grand Canal cover an area of one hundred thousand square li and have a population of over ten million. They rely entirely on the east and west dikes for protection. This time, the entire Grand Canal was impacted and severely damaged by the water. The earthworks repair is urgent and must be completed quickly. However, some areas may not be solid enough, requiring reconstruction. The Gaobao and Jiangdu sections of the west dike, as well as the Laisheng'an section of the east dike, which are being assisted by your committee, account for less than two-tenths of the entire project. The overestimation of costs and the difficulties of the work should be carefully considered. Currently, eight-tenths of the entire project will be completed, but there is still a shortage of over five hundred and fifty thousand yuan. Work has been suspended pending the arrival of funds. With the water level rising slightly, the overall situation is extremely worrying. According to National Government Instruction No. 510 of the twentieth year of the Republic, "This year's floods have caused multiple breaches in the Grand Canal dikes. The twelfth regular meeting of this government resolved to allocate one million yuan in cash from the Relief Committee for Disaster Relief to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to quickly handle the Grand Canal dike repair project." Furthermore, Central Government Instruction No. 579 approved the early allocation of funds from the additional levies on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and other locations. Therefore, your committee has the authority to allocate these funds. As for the Provincial Government's borrowing of 10,000 tons of American flour from your committee to finance the Grand Canal project, this is a separate matter that will be repaid with construction bonds on a fixed schedule. To date, we have only received 545,000 yuan. We urgently hope that your committee will quickly allocate the remaining funds to assist the project. Currently, the people of the ten counties north of the Yangtze River suffered a terrible water disaster last year. Countless people died not from drowning but from starvation. In recent months, they have been able to work the land in a state of groaning and distress, hoping that the repair of the Grand Canal dikes will be completed soon. If work is suspended due to lack of funds, resulting in another catastrophe, then the overall situation in Jiangsu will be unbearable to witness. You, Director, are a native of Jiangsu and are dedicated to your duties. You must be determined to complete the Grand Canal dike repair project as soon as possible. We urge you to report to your committee and immediately allocate the central government funds to the Provincial Government for distribution to the project sites to avoid danger caused by suspending work and waiting for funds. In addition to sending letters to Mr. Huang Renzhi, Jiang Wenyu, and Zhu Dexuan to convey everything in person, we are sending this telegram for your consideration. We hope that you will understand. Standing Committee of the Post-Disaster Relief Association for the Huai Dike Water Disaster in Northern Jiangsu, Han Guojun, Ma Shijie, etc.

Zeng Yangfu, Director of Zhejiang Construction Department, Comes to Shanghai 116

Continuing to Negotiate Loan for Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway

Zeng Yangfu, Commissioner of Zhejiang Province and Director of the Construction Department, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to continue negotiating all matters with the Qixin Banking Syndicate in order to finalize the loan for the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. The Huadong News Agency reporter specially interviewed Mr. Zeng at his hotel. According to him, the progress of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and the methods for relieving new and old cocoon silk and issuing loans were quite detailed. The following is a record of the situation:

Loan for the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway According to Mr. Zeng, the original plan for completing the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway was to continue construction from Jinhua, passing through Tangxi and other three counties, and reaching Jiangshan. The section of highway from Jiangshan County to Guangfeng, Jiangxi, has already been built and can be connected. Regarding the counties from Jiangshan to the Fujian border, the Zhejiang Provincial Government has consulted with the Fujian Provincial Government to jointly construct it to facilitate the suppression of bandits. Therefore, the completion of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway is of great importance to the security of Zhejiang and eastern Jiangxi and northern Fujian. From Jinhua to Jiangshan, the entire line is approximately 168 kilometers long. The estimated cost for construction and materials is 7 million yuan. However, the construction funds for Zhejiang Province are only 300,000 yuan per year, so it is necessary to raise funds. Recently, Du Zhenyuan, Director of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Bureau, went to Beijing specifically for this matter to negotiate a 200,000 pound Gengzi Indemnity loan (approximately 3.4 million Chinese currency). Zhu Jiaju, Chairman of the Gengzi Indemnity Committee, has already approved it. My visit to Shanghai this time is related to project funding. I plan to transfer the Hangzhou Power Plant to the Qixin Banking Syndicate, which could yield 1 million yuan. The banking syndicate has informally approved it. However, the banking syndicate requires an interest rate of over 1%, while I advocate a maximum of 1%. After further negotiations, a satisfactory agreement can be reached.

Relief for Old Cocoons and Old Silk Regarding the promotion and sale of old cocoons and old silk from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, the Construction Department previously consulted with the Jiangsu Industrial Department and agreed to allocate 4 million taels of silver to subsidize silk cocoon merchants in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to cover the losses from promoting and selling old cocoons and old silk. However, the Zhejiang provincial treasury is extremely strained. However, relieving the current decline in silk cocoons is an urgent matter. Therefore, I drafted a plan, consulted with Jiangsu Province, and issued a relief silk cocoon treasury bond of 2.2 million taels, starting on June 1, 21st year of the Republic, with a monthly interest rate of 0.5%, and a term of 50 months, with full repayment of principal and interest. Zhejiang Province will use the 150,000 yuan in funds monthly allocated to the province by the central government due to the reduction in levies as a guarantee fund. This plan has been submitted by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to the Ministry of Finance. I previously came to Shanghai once for this purpose. The Minister of Finance, Song Ziwen, has agreed to the issuance of treasury bonds and relief of silk cocoons. The Ministry of Finance has also telegraphed Zhejiang Province, approving the issuance. However, the articles of association and repayment schedule must be submitted by the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan for consultation with the Legislative Yuan for formal approval before they can be implemented.

Relief for New Silk and New Cocoons Regarding the issue of relieving new cocoons and new silk, I previously consulted with the Zhejiang business community and raised 1.8 million yuan, which was entrusted to various banks and money shops to lend to cocoon businesses in various places. The government and businesses jointly organized the Zhejiang Provincial Cocoon Loan Pledge Committee to handle the pledging of cocoon loans. In addition to Hangzhou cocoon leaves, cocoon merchants from other counties and regions can come to the province to borrow money from the Pledge Committee to purchase cocoons. The original procedure for borrowing money required cocoon merchants to provide 40% cash as a guarantee and use the loan of 40% to collect 60% of the dry cocoons as collateral. This year, the spring cocoons are withering and unable to operate, plunging to a thousand zhang. Originally intended to relieve the cocoon industry, the regulations have been changed to show consideration for cocoon merchants, and consulted with the Department of Finance, and the provision for Jiang Cocoon Merchants to find a guarantee and supply 40% of cash has been changed to 30%. The two departments have ordered the Zhejiang Cocoon Loan Pledge Committee to comply, etc.

Fuyuhui's Amended Articles Approved by the Executive Yuan for Record 124

Following Approval of Amended Articles

The "Relief Association for Families of Martyrs Who Died for the Country" received Official Letter No. 1961 from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan yesterday, approving the Ministry of Interior's Official Letter No. 33. The letter stated, "With regards to your dispatch No. 1703, the President's instruction is: The memorial submitted by Xu Shiying and other standing committee members of the 'Relief Association for Families of Martyrs Who Died for the Country' regarding the drafting of articles of association and requesting review and filing should be submitted to the Ministry of Interior for discussion and reply." Accordingly, a copy of the original document is enclosed for your reference. Also enclosed is the original memorial and a copy of the articles of association. After review, the nineteen articles of association proposed by the association are generally feasible. However, Article 4, Section 1, states that old folks' homes are easily confused with those established by relief institutions in various provinces and cities. For the sake of honoring the direct elders of martyrs who died for the country, it is suggested that the name be changed to "Respect for Elders Home" to show encouragement and virtue. Article 2, Section 2, which refers to the "Hall of Pure Virtue," conflicts with the second article of the "Regulations on Commendation." It is suggested to change it to "Hall of Consolation" to express the meaning of consolation. Also, the phrase "charity halls" under the "Hall of Pure Virtue" or similar organizations should be changed to "charitable organizations." In Article 3, Section 3, the phrase "those with excellent grades can be further trained" is changed to "children of revolutionary meritorious personnel should be handled in accordance with the regulations on tuition fees" to show preferential treatment. In Article 5, the last paragraph, "teach them agricultural affairs," is changed to "teach them agricultural skills" to be more explicit. Are these suggestions appropriate? We are replying for your review and submission, etc. This has been approved. The President's instruction is: Approved as requested by the Ministry of Interior. The "Relief Association for Families of Martyrs Who Died for the Country" and the Ministry of Interior should be informed separately. Apart from sending separate notices, this letter is for your information, etc. It is now reported that the association has amended each point as instructed by the Ministry of Interior and has submitted it to the Executive Yuan for filing.

Public Letter from All Coal Dealers in the French Concession 125

Requesting the Revocation of the Order and the Cancellation of the Business Tax

The new "Regulations for the Management of Hard Fuels" promulgated by the French Concession Municipal Council, which levies a business tax, has already prompted the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Coal Industry Association, and the New West District 12th Road Business Association of the French Concession to successively send letters to the French Concession Municipal Council, requesting them to consider the merchants' difficulties, revoke the order, and cancel the business tax to alleviate the merchants' plight. This has been reported in previous news. It is now known that all the coal dealers in the French Concession, including Jin Shun, Xin Shun, Yi Shunxing, Yi Hexing, Xin Da, Xie Taicheng Ji, Kailin, Sen Shun, Xiang He, Yan Jing, Ping Ping, Zhi Cheng, Lao Qia Yuan, Tong Fu, Qian Shunchang, Qian Dachang, Xie He Shun, Gong Changxin, Rong Tai, Da Feng Yong, Song Tai, Gong Changyu, Zhe Tai Xie Ji, Wan Xing, Xiang Tai, Lao Jiu Da, Tong Tai, Qian Feng, Shun Xing, Shun Cheng, Xin Kang, Qia Sheng, Qi Tai, Feng Tai, Piao Zhao Shun, Wu Taixing, Jin Taixiang, Da Xing, Xing Long, Pu Da, Song Sheng, Shun Xin, Tai Xingyi, Xiang Xin, Lao Qian Yuan, Sen Kang, Yong Sheng, Qian Cheng, Xie Chang, He Fa, Tong Li, Xin Chang, Ye Sen Tai, Tang Longchang, Yong Li, Qian Fengxiang, Sen Tai, Xing Sheng, Yuan Chang, Tian Cheng, Yi Tai, Yuan Tai, Qing Tai, Yang Ji, Hong Tai, Yuan Tai, Sen Chang, Mao Chang, Yuan Da, Fu Chang Tai, Sen Tai Hua Ji, Xiang Da, Tong Yuanxiang, Cheng Chang, Qian Wan Yuan, Jin Tai, Yu Cheng, Shun Tai, Yuan Sheng, Xie Chang, Xin Xing, Ju Kang, Shi Wanxing, Yuan Mao, Qian Da You, Ji Feng, Ji Tai, Shun Chang, Sen Da, Yong Changxiang, Xin Tai, Shun Tai, Yong Tai, Qian Wan Yuan, and more than 200 other companies, collectively presented a letter to the General Manager of the French Concession Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "We are requesting the revocation of the order and the cancellation of the business tax on hard fuels to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and stabilize business operations. Coal dealers have established businesses in the French Concession, formally paying taxes, and struggling to maintain operations. Unexpectedly, your office has promulgated new regulations for the management of hard fuels (coal, coal balls, and firewood, etc.) in warehouses or stores, requiring the payment of an investigation fee of two yuan and a license fee of three yuan every six months. This business tax is about to be implemented and collected. The coal business (i.e., operating hard fuels) has low profits and high expenses. It is well known that business is only booming in the winter and depressed in the summer. The coal dealers are not able to afford the business tax. Moreover, such a business tax is unprecedented in the Chinese Concession and the International Settlement, and is also a new thing in the French Concession. Furthermore, hard fuels are daily necessities for residents. Therefore, in the business tax rate table formulated by the Chinese Concession Municipal Government, only the coal ball industry is taxed at one-thousandth, and coal is not taxed. If your office insists on implementing the business tax, it will directly increase the burden on coal dealers and indirectly affect the livelihood of the people. It will also force all coal dealers operating hard fuels in the French Concession to move to the Chinese Concession or the International Settlement. The coal dealers feel that the regulations are difficult to bear and that the tax is impractical. Therefore, we jointly sign and seal this letter, urging your office to consider the merchants' difficulties, revoke the order, and cancel the harsh hard fuel business tax to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and stabilize business operations. We implore you to review and implement this request and to grant a reply to the leading coal dealers to reassure the people and comfort the public. Respectfully submitted to the General Manager of the French Concession Municipal Council in Shanghai."

Lawsuit After the Closure of Zheng Yi Bank 126

Creditor Wins Lawsuit in Trial

Zhengyi Bank on Jiangxi Road declared bankruptcy on November 19, 1920. Various firms that had deposits with the bank demanded compensation, but were refused on the grounds that the bank was a limited company. As a result, the creditors formed the Zhenggyi Bank Creditors' Association and elected Qian Xuanqing as their representative to sue the chairman of the board of Zhenggyi Bank, Ye Hongying, and others in the Shanghai First Special District Court, requesting repayment of the debts. On June 14, at 2 p.m., the presiding judge, Xiao Xiebin, took the bench in the seventh courtroom. The plaintiff representative, Qian Xuanqing, along with the attorneys Hu Jue and Chou Kaizuo, appeared in court. The defendants, Ye Hongying, and others, did not appear, but their attorneys, Wei Wenhan and Wu Guochang, did. After a lengthy debate, the plaintiff's attorney, Hu Jue, presented documents from the Ministry of Industry and the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, which stated that the Zhenggyi Bank had obtained its business license from the Ministry of Finance and had not legally obtained a limited company license from the Ministry of Industry. Therefore, it was naturally a partnership. The distinction between limited and unlimited liability should be based on the Company Law, which went into effect on July 2, 1931. Since the defendant did not obtain a license from the Ministry of Industry or register with the Bureau of Social Affairs, which is the competent authority, and report to the Ministry of Industry for a license, as required by Article 21 of the Company Law, the defendant's reliance on the illegal license issued by the Shanghai County Magistrate's Office and the Financial Supervision Administration of the Ministry of Finance is legally baseless. The business license allows both limited and unlimited liability companies to operate. The plaintiff's legal and evidentiary submissions are sufficient to prove that the defendant is a partnership and should be jointly and severally liable for the plaintiff's debt of 33,635.22 yuan and the statutory interest for the delay. The defendant's attorneys, Wei Wenhan and Wu Guochang, argued that the defendant was a limited company and had a license from the Shanghai Public Concession Financial Supervision Administration of the Ministry of Finance. They requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected. The court announced that the judgment would be pronounced at 1 p.m. on June 20. The judgment was pronounced at 2 p.m. on the afternoon of the previous day. The main points were that the defendant should repay the plaintiff 19,143.1 taels of silver, which should be offset by the assets of Zhenggyi Bank. If the assets are insufficient, the defendants are jointly and severally liable for the remaining amount, and the statutory interest for the delay shall be calculated from November 19 of last year until the end of the execution. The remainder of the plaintiff's requests was rejected, and the litigation costs were borne by the defendant.

Ye Shantao Appeals Case of Being Accused of Forging Documents 129

Debate Concluded Yesterday

Judgment Set for the 27th

The case of Ye Shantao, Zhang Zhengji, Zhu Chengfei and others forging documents was previously litigated in the First Special District Court. The initial trial ruled that the plaintiff's evidence was insufficient and that Ye was not guilty. Subsequently, an appeal was filed with the Second Branch of the High Court, which also held several hearings. The focus of the dispute was whether Ye Shantao was a director of the Gongfa Company founded by Huang Chu Jiu. Ye wanted to prove that he was not a director of Gongfa Company, so he presented a letter from Huang Chu Jiu withdrawing Ye's directorship. This letter was not written by Huang himself but by his secretary. Therefore, Zhang Zhengji and others suspected that Ye had forged it after Huang's death. Therefore, they filed a lawsuit for the crime of forging documents. At the last court hearing, the plaintiff insisted that the court obtain the director's meeting minutes from the High Court branch to prove that Ye had indeed received director's fees. Yesterday was another court hearing, and both parties appeared in court to be examined. As the evidence in the case was complete and the trial had been held several times, the facts of the case were clear. Therefore, the judge briefly questioned both parties and then began the debate. The lawyer Yan, representing the appellant, first stated that the case began after the Gongfa Company, founded by Huang Chu Jiu, went bankrupt and no assets were found. After liquidation, each creditor could only receive 20%, and the remaining amount could only be claimed from its directors. Ye wanted to avoid the responsibility of being a director, so he presented a letter from Huang to him. Whether the letter was written by Huang himself has been proven to be false. Furthermore, the director must obtain the approval of the board of directors to withdraw. However, there is no resolution on Huang's withdrawal in the board minutes. Furthermore, the letter from Huang Chu Jiu to Gan Yuesong was also written by the secretary, and the handwriting of the two letters is the same. Therefore, it is necessary to clarify that the letter from Huang to Gan is an ordinary commercial correspondence. Why is it not personally signed and sealed to resign from his directorship? As for Ye's claim that he was a director because he had lost 300,000 yuan with Huang in the exchange and was given the title of director, with a monthly fee of 40 yuan to compensate for his loss, it is not possible to compensate for his 300,000 yuan loss by paying 40 yuan a month for a thousand years, etc. The lawyer Lu Shaoxu, representing the respondent, then argued that at the court hearing in early spring, the plaintiff stated that he did not know whether the letter of resignation was true or false. Therefore, the purpose of his prosecution for forging documents was lost. The minutes obtained from the High Court branch showed that Ye was indeed named in the minutes before 1927, but not after that. Furthermore, the Gongfa Company's directors were limited to nine people, and three supervisors. This number was already complete. If Ye Shantao was added, wouldn't there be ten directors? Furthermore, the letter of resignation was written in 1927. How could Ye know that there would be litigation in the future and forge a letter in advance to shirk responsibility? As it was late, the court announced the end of the debate and set the judgment for the 27th of this month. If either party has any further comments, they may submit supplementary briefs within three days.

Trial Opened Yesterday, No Spectators Allowed

Ye Qinghe Implicated in Japanese Morphine Manufacturing Case 131

Ye Arrested in Sanatorium

Ordered to Pay 30,000 Yuan Bail

The Japanese-run morphine manufacturing plant set up by Nakamura at No. 18 Sandefang, Xijiaxing Road, Hongkou, was discovered by Chief Detective Wang Changgen of the Public Concession Police Department's General Inspection Office on the 23rd of last month. Together with Western Detective Pan Gengquan, they went to Nakamura's residence to arrest him and handed him over to the Japanese Consulate for trial. They also arrested nine Chinese persons, including Fang Yinbao, Su Ahui, and Diao Jinsheng. Morphine drugs and equipment were seized and transferred to the First Special District Court for investigation. Wang Kaiyan, a staff member in the organ, was released without charge. The other eight persons, including Fang Yinbao, were sentenced to imprisonment and fines, as reported in detail in the newspapers. However, Ye Qinghe from Fujian, the mastermind of the case, was still at large. It was discovered by Detective Wang Changgen, who was handling the case, that Ye had checked into Room 208 of the Chinese-Western Sanatorium on Rue de la Gare in the French Concession and was registered under a citizen's name. On the night of the 4th of this month, he worked with detectives from the French Concession Police Department to arrest Ye and hand him over to the Second Special District Court for interrogation. He was released on bail pending trial. The First Special District Court issued a warrant the other day, ordering the judicial police to bring Ye back. Yesterday morning, he was brought before the First High Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the facts of the case, saying that the defendant, Ye Qinghe, opened Guomin Pharmacy in the French Concession, and that Fang Yin, etc., who had already been punished, were partners in the pharmacy. On the 3rd of this month, the defendant took a yellow car and used the alias Shen, signing in Western script, claiming to be in the hospital for medical treatment. When the police sent detectives to Xijiaxing Road to solve the case, they found envelopes, stationery, etc., all with the words "Guomin Pharmacy." There is now a witness, Wang Jinyan, who used to work in the private morphine manufacturing plant set up by the defendant, so he knows the defendant's name, and he committed robbery of opium at the former Mixed Court. Wang Jinyan testified that he was a tinsmith and had worked in the morphine factory set up by the defendant at No. 15 Jiaye Road, Great World, so he knew it. After the factory moved, he went there once. Ye Qinghe confessed that he was one of the shareholders of Guomin Pharmacy and did not know Fang Yinbao. The person in charge was Jin Jinhua. He knew nothing about morphine manufacturing. He also retained lawyer Jiang Yiping to apply for bail. Judge Qiao Wanxuan reviewed the confession and ordered the defendant Ye Qinghe to pay 30,000 yuan bail pending another trial.

Judgment in Substandard and Counterfeit Goods Case 132

Gu Zhengda Sentenced to Three Months

Fine of Three Thousand Yuan

Meilun Weaving Factory and Hongzhang Dyeing Factory reported that Zhenkang Cloth Store on Xiamen Road was selling substandard goods under the brand names of the two factories. The police were notified and sent detectives to Zhenkang Store, where they seized many boxes of cloth and arrested Gu Zhengda, a partner in the store, and handed him over to the First Special District Court on charges of obstructing agriculture, industry, and commerce. This has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge opened the court to continue the trial. According to Gu Zhengda's confession, the Hongzhang labels affixed to the cloth boxes were because the cloth in the boxes was dyed by Hongzhang and was not counterfeit. The cloth had been mortgaged to the Tongchun Qianzhuang on Tianjin Road. Yu Futian, the representative of Tongchun Qianzhuang, and lawyer Wu Linkun appeared in court, stating that the Zhenkang cloth pledged to them was introduced by Gu Disheng of Desheng Cotton Cloth Store and was processed legally. Subsequently, the defendant's defense lawyer Fan Gang presented the transaction contract between Zhenkang and Meilun Factory, proving that Zhenkang's cloth was indeed purchased from Meilun. Gu Zhengda continued to confess that this time was actually because Lu Junhui of Hongzhang hated him for not contacting him for transactions, so he could not get a commission, which led to this case. However, according to the Xia representative of Meilun, they had transactions with Zhenkang last year. This year, the cloth sold to Zhenkang was bleached striped cloth. Lu Junhui of Hongzhang admitted to dyeing the cloth for Zhenkang but denied putting the labels on the dyed cloth. Finally, the police lawyer Hu Jiabao, the two plaintiffs' lawyers Chen Tingrui, and the defendant's lawyer debated with each other to the end. Judge Ge immediately pronounced judgment in court, sentencing Gu Zhengda to three months in prison and fining him one thousand yuan. If he is unable to pay, he may be imprisoned for one day for every three yuan, but not more than one year. The cloth and other items were confiscated. The defendant, upon hearing the judgment, expressed dissatisfaction and his lawyer Fan Gang immediately declared an appeal, which was granted by the judge. The police were ordered to take Gu back to the police station for verification.

Meeting of the Postal Workers' Union 134

For the sake of comprehensively promoting union affairs and consolidating the foundation of the union, the local Postal Workers' Union held a general membership meeting at 10:30 AM yesterday in the courtyard of the Postal Administration Bureau. More than two thousand members attended. Zhang Kechang, Xiao Qingshan, and Zhu Yinghua were publicly elected as the presidium, with Shi Jiuyuan serving as the recorder. The order of the meeting was extremely [orderly]. The presidium reported on the purpose of the meeting and union affairs, leading to the discussion and resolution of several important motions. (1) Regarding illegal organizations established under the guise of the Postal Workers' Union, all members of the union shall deny their legitimacy and strictly suppress them. It was resolved to pass the motion and notify the authorities. Hereafter, in addition to not accepting any communication from illegal organizations established under the name of this union, the main actors in illegal organizations shall be subject to the most severe punishment according to postal regulations. (2) To expel labor traitors such as Xing Rongzhao, Sun Hanliang, Tan Changde, and Zhao Liancheng, who are disrupting the Postal Workers' Union. It was resolved that, based on the resolution of the delegates' conference, the Executive and Supervisory Committee shall be responsible for immediately expelling these labor traitors. All members of the union, united in hatred, will never work with these labor traitors and demand that the authorities not allow these labor traitors to work in the bureau. (3) Regarding how the union should respond to the actions of a certain department's (secret) authorities, who have insulted laborers, disrupted the labor movement, damaged the postal service, behaved perversely, acted basely, bought off labor traitors, and disrupted the union, resulting in obvious crimes. It was resolved that (a) the Executive Committee shall take the most effective methods and means to deal with it when necessary; (b) the facts shall be announced to inform all sectors of society that the disruption by labor traitors is by no means an internal dispute of the union, but a vile plan by a certain department's authorities to sabotage the entire postal service; (c) the National Postal Workers' General Union shall be petitioned to issue a circular to postal workers' unions in various regions to take unified action. (4) To request the Postal Economic System Research Committee to convene a meeting as soon as possible and implement a plan to consolidate the foundation of the postal service. It was resolved to pass the motion and instruct the Executive Committee to handle it. (5) To convene the 10th Representatives' Conference of the union as soon as possible to elect the 10th Executive and Supervisory Committee. It was resolved to pass the motion and instruct the Executive Committee to handle it as soon as possible. (6) To have Zou Zhong issue a declaration of the conference. It was resolved to pass other important motions. Finally, slogans were shouted, and the meeting adjourned at 12:00 noon. In addition, on the morning of the 20th at 10:00 AM, more than ten members of the union's Executive and Supervisory Committee went to the Postal General Bureau to petition Director Huang Naishu, requesting three points: (1) The General Bureau hastily accepted letters from the so-called "Three-Five Labor Traitors," who had privately established an illegal "Joint Office," and instructed the Shanghai Bureau to investigate. This is procedurally inappropriate and suggests collusion with labor traitors. It is requested that this be clarified and corrected. (2) Xing Rongzhao and nine others who have already been expelled from the union should be promptly removed from the Postal Bureau. (3) Regarding the few individuals who participated in the closed-down illegal organization, since they have violated national law, please clarify how the Bureau should punish them according to postal regulations. At that time, Director Huang promised that, regarding the first point, he would issue a clear order to the Shanghai Bureau to immediately cancel the previous instruction and declare that hereafter, the Bureau would not accept any illegal organization established under the name of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union. This order was personally drafted by the Director in front of the union representatives at 10:00 AM this morning and handed over to the secretary for issuance. As for items (2) and (3), to avoid future disputes in the postal service, Director Huang sincerely expressed to the union representatives that he would consider a compromise solution, that is, to transfer the main elements of the illegal organization away from Shanghai first, but for the sake of prudence, he would simultaneously send a telegram to the ministry for instructions. It was heard that when the Director's reception room was discussing the matter yesterday morning, hundreds of union members also went to the outside of the Director's office to await a reply. This morning, when negotiations continued in the Director's office, Mr. Chen Kecheng, secretary of the municipal government, was also present and expressed sympathy for this compromise solution.

Inspection Report of the Central Bank 135

Report of the 128th Inspection

The 128th inspection report of the Central Bank's issuance reserve states: This council is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank, in accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. On June 20, 1932, Supervisor Qia Qing held the 128th inspection at the Issuing Bureau of this bank. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 29,092,376 silver dollars, including 26,261,977 silver dollar notes and 2,830,397 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of the convertible notes reserve is 29,092,376 silver dollars, including 23,572,942 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 20,961,970.81 silver dollars stored in this bank's issuing vault, 1,458,629 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,152,342.19 silver dollars stored with fellow banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 5,519,434 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 375,000 customs gold units. The total amount of the customs gold convertible notes reserve is 375,000 customs gold units. This reserve includes 150,000 US dollars stored with fellow banks in this port, valued at 40 customs gold units each, as above. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, the cash reserve should be 60% and the guarantee reserve 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. June 20, 1932, Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank.

"Elopement" Actress Sues for Loss of Virginity 136

Virginity Lost Before Age Sixteen

Sues in Court Seeking $50,000 in Damages

Defendant Gu Baosen is an Architect

Failed to Appear in Court Yesterday, Arrest Warrant to be Issued

Tan Ying, a female actress of the Lianhua Film Company who plays the lead role in the elopement film directed by Du Yu, has been praised by critics as a rising star in the film industry. Unexpectedly, she has experienced a similar situation as in the elopement film, which can be described as coincidental. Tan Ying, along with her mother Tan Wang, hired lawyers Zhang Chongding and Xu Qinpu and, as residents of No. 5, Yude Alley, East Tangjia Lane, filed a criminal self-accusation with the local court against Gu Baolin, also known as Gu Xiaochun, an architect, accusing him of seducing a young girl. The self-accusation stated that he seduced a girl under the age of sixteen and requested legal punishment, with accompanying civil proceedings. The self-accuser and the defendant were previously landlord and tenant and lived together for two years, so they knew each other. The defendant often visited the self-accuser's residence and, seeing that the self-accuser's daughter, Da Bao, also known as Tan Ying, had grown up and was attractive, developed covetous thoughts and seduced her in every possible way. The self-accuser's daughter, lacking in knowledge, was seduced and, on April 5 of this year, designed to seduce her and have physical relations. Moreover, the defendant's boldness was as great as the sky, and he actually lured the self-accuser's daughter to his home in Tangjia Lane. The self-accuser's daughter, seeing that the defendant already had a wife, Tang Jianchun, realized she had been deceived and was in great pain. The defendant comforted her, saying he would definitely divorce Tang. This was delayed until late May, when he produced a divorce certificate

and a Shen Bao advertisement. The self-accuser's daughter realized that Tang was still at Gu's home and that the divorce was actually a farce, nothing more than a means to deceive her into marriage. She suddenly woke up and returned to the self-accuser to cry and tell the truth. The self-accuser was extremely angry and, accompanied by her daughter, went to the defendant's residence to negotiate. The defendant spoke sweet words, insisting that he sincerely wanted to marry the self-accuser's daughter and that the divorce from Tang was real. He even voluntarily wrote a note stating that if any disputes arose with the Tang family in the future, he would be willing to pay $50,000 (this was presented for inspection at the trial). The self-accuser realized that this matter could not be resolved through words and accepted the note written by the defendant and took her daughter home. After questioning, it was learned that the defendant had also engaged in intimidation, saying that if she did not agree to marry him, he would stab her to death with a knife. Thinking that the self-accuser's daughter, Tan Ying, also known as Da Bao, is habitually said to be seventeen years old, born on April 22 of the lunar calendar, and legally deducting the age, she is still under sixteen years old. Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code stipulates that sexual intercourse with a girl under the age of sixteen is considered rape. The defendant's seduction of the self-accuser's daughter actually began on April 5, before her sixteenth birthday. According to law, she was only fifteen years old. The defendant took advantage of a weak girl whose knowledge had not reached adulthood and whose body had not fully developed, using wealth and power to seduce her into marriage in order to achieve his lascivious purpose, causing the virgin's chastity to be trampled upon. This is tolerable, what is not tolerable? Therefore, in accordance with Article 337 and Paragraph 2 of the same article of the Criminal Procedure Law, a self-accusation is filed, requesting the court to punish the defendant with the appropriate crime according to Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. Furthermore, the self-accuser's daughter suffered physical and mental pain as a result of this misfortune and is bound by social traditions and her own concept of chastity, making it impossible for her to remarry. The cost of living and irreparable damage she has suffered should be compensated by the defendant. Moreover, the self-accuser's daughter works as an actress at the Lianhua Film Company, earning a monthly salary of $120, as evidenced by a contract. Calculated over thirty years, this amounts to $43,000. Therefore, in the accompanying civil proceedings, it is requested that the court order compensation for a total of $50,000, which is fair and convenient, etc. This case was heard yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM by Judge Shi in the first courtroom. Tan Wang and Tan Ying testified to the same facts as above. The judge instructed that the defendant, Gu Baosen, also known as Gu Xiaochun, refused to accept the subpoena. Asked what the self-accusers requested, lawyers Zhang and Gu stated that the defendant was intentionally evading and requested an arrest warrant. The judge approved this and ordered the defendant to be arrested and brought to court for further investigation before adjourning.

A Couple Commits Suicide in a Hotel 137

Found Lifeless

A Couple Lying Side by Side, Stiff

A Long Suicide Note

Incomprehensible Poems on the Wall

A hotel at No. 348, Tianjin Road, had a male and female guest check in on the evening of March 19, booking room 412. The man claimed his name was Lü Zhongyi, 26 years old, a merchant. The woman was about the same age, spoke with a Suzhou accent, and both came from Hangzhou. The two kept to themselves, but their behavior suggested a close relationship. Around noon the day before, they called for a tea boy to buy a pack of chewing gum. About two hours later, they ordered a plate of curry chicken rice. At that time, they told the waiter that they would continue to rent the room. After the two finished eating, they went out together and only returned in the evening. After entering the room, they closed the door tightly, and there was no sound. Until yesterday afternoon, the tea boys had cleaned all the rooms on the fourth floor, except for room 412, which remained silent. It was already 12:30 PM, so the foreman called out the guest's name outside the room, but there was no response after a long time. So he used a key to open the door, only to see the curtains drawn, and the room was unusually dim. He turned on the light and saw a couple lying side by side on the bed, stiff and lifeless. The accounting room was immediately notified, and the Old Gate Police Station was contacted to send detectives to investigate. The two were then taken to Renji Hospital, where they were confirmed to have died from poisoning and were transferred to the morgue to await inspection by the court. The deceased left a suicide note on the table, which was lengthy and extensive, but unfortunately, the writing was not very coherent. It described the deceased's background and the reasons for their despondency. Before taking their lives, the two also wrote several short sentences on the wall, which are recorded as follows: "Dying for the country is not resolute, I hope you don't resent my death, I am fortunate. I am a person full of hatred in this world, this man is especially affectionate to me, not sparing a feather. You are in the misty mountain, I hope people leave, I will be a wave-cresting subject in the flood. You are going to death, do you know? After you, there will be no affection, in fact, I am also going to death, do you know?" These lines are like poetry but not poetry. A photo of the man and woman together was also found in the room, along with the words "Nantong Jiangsu Bank," indicating that the man and woman died for love.

The Truth About the Dutch Ship Fire 141

Losses Amount to $300,000

Fire Caused by Collision of Sulfur

The incident of the Dutch cargo ship Seroskerk, managed by the Java Shipping Company of this port, accidentally catching fire has been reported in this newspaper. The truth about the fire and the amount of loss are now further investigated and recorded as follows:

Moving Sulfur Causes Disaster: The ship was loaded with more than 5,000 tons of cargo from various ports in the Netherlands and Germany. The third hold contained 50 pieces of sulfur, which were loaded into the hold as military supplies. This sulfur is most likely to cause accidents. Excessive dryness or humidity can easily cause explosions. When the coolies were unloading the sulfur, one package was standing upright on top of the other sulfur packages. The foreign officer supervising the unloading of the cargo was afraid that it would fall and collide, causing a fire, so he went to support it and laid it horizontally on the cargo. Unexpectedly, due to a moment of carelessness, the package of sulfur collided violently with a bag below, causing a loud bang, sparks flying, and black smoke rising. Fortunately, the workers quickly escaped and were not harmed. The fire broke out in an instant, and the flames were extremely fierce. The shipowner was notified and immediately ordered the third hold where the fire broke out to be sealed off quickly to prevent the flames from spreading out.

Cargo in Three Holds Completely Destroyed: Fire trucks from the dock and fireboats from the Customs arrived. The shipowner immediately ordered the hold to be opened to allow water to be sprayed to extinguish the fire. Unexpectedly, when the hold was opened, water overflowed and directly penetrated the fourth hold, burning the cargo it encountered. The shipowner closed the fourth hold again. When the fourth hold was opened, the fire penetrated the fifth hold. As a result, the man-made silk, fertilizer, hardware, paper, sulfur, etc. that were carried were all reduced to ashes. The cargo that was not burned was also soaked in water. After six and a half hours, the fire was finally extinguished. The total cargo loss is at least more than $200,000.

Unloading the Soaked Cargo to Inspect the Damage: Yesterday, the company ordered the shipowner to pump out the accumulated water from the third, fourth, and fifth holds. All the remaining embers and water-soaked cargo were ordered to be stored on the Blue Funnel Wharf. On the one hand, customers were notified, and on the other hand, a public surveyor, Ellis, was invited to inspect the losses and prepare to auction off the water-soaked cargo. Currently, the water is being drained first. All the cargo from Dalian, Qinhuangdao, and Japan that was not burned on the ship will be transferred to other ships.

Ship Body to Be Overhauled in the Factory: After the great fire in the third, fourth, and fifth holds, the structural integrity of the ship was completely destroyed and could no longer be used. Now, after unloading the cargo, the ship will be towed to the Ruirong Shipyard for a major overhaul. The three hatchways were burned, and the repair costs will also be 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. The ship was originally scheduled to go to North China and Japan today, but it will no longer be sailing there. It will take at least two weeks to leave the dock and set sail. All the losses of cargo and the ship's body in this fire are covered by insurance, and the insurance company will be responsible for all compensation.

Chaplin's Brother Leaves Shanghai 142

Declines All Social Engagements

Proceeds Directly to Marseille

Charlie Chaplin and his brother Sydney Chaplin, both comedic stars of the American film industry, are renowned on the silver screen and famous throughout the world. The two brothers have come to the Far East to tour and study theater and music. Charlie Chaplin has finished his tour of Japan and originally planned to return to the United States by ship. However, because the Pacific Ocean was too rough, he changed his route to Europe via the Suez Canal and then across the Atlantic Ocean back to Hollywood in the United States. Charlie, along with Edward Angue, a member of the film industry, and Laning Shimei, a violin expert, arrived in Shanghai from Kobe, Japan, on the Nippon Yusen Kaisha's Terukuni Maru. When they arrived at the port, many reporters came to the ship to take pictures and talk to them. Mr. Charlie Chaplin declined all social engagements and did not respond to the representatives sent by various cinemas in Shanghai to welcome him. Later, he went ashore alone for a short tour and then returned to the original ship. This trip proceeds directly to Marseille, France, but he will also have to go ashore in Hong Kong.

Lake Society Calls on All Sectors to Promote Domestic Silk 143

The Lake Society Committee sent letters to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Citizens' Federation, and various domestic goods organizations yesterday to promote domestic silk. We are writing to inform you that, according to a letter from our society member Gao Weisong, the silk produced in our Lake area has always been a major commodity, on which the nation's tax revenue and the people's livelihood mutually depend. In recent years, imported goods have flooded the market, and silk trade in various countries has risen like a storm, resulting in a sharp decline in the sales of our silk, which has always been known for its natural wealth, compared to the past. This is an unprecedented phenomenon. The distant cause of this is that we adhere to old methods and do not know how to improve. Last year's silk cocoons have not been cleared, and this year's new products are accumulating again. Although we are fortunate to have gentlemen in Shanghai discussing methods to promote the new and get rid of the old and request government subsidies, the industry is benefiting from this great favor, like receiving timely rain, but relying on temporary relief is not a fundamental solution. The society member, aware of this crisis, is deeply concerned and is seeking a remedy to save the desperate situation. After searching day and night, he has somewhat achieved his wish. He has now invented yarn silks such as Xishi Ge. This kind of material is specially selected from top-quality factories and employs famous masters to process and weave it densely, making it comparable to imported goods. This is just the beginning of improving silk, and it is by no means comparable to those who use it as a pretext for speculation. This ambition and this heart can be testified by heaven and earth. However, at the beginning of the invention, sponsorship is needed to show people's faith and to promote it. We specially rely on your esteemed committee, which is the mouthpiece of our hometown and has a well-deserved reputation, and dare to ask you to promote it, etc., and send a sample of the silk. We have found that this type of silk is of excellent quality and has a novel pattern, without any inferior silk or artificial silk mixed in. The price is also very modest in order to resist foreign goods, which is very suitable. At this time, when Shanghai is in urgent need of revival, all Chinese people have the duty to protect their rights and interests. With this improved silk, we should do our best to promote it. We have always admired your association's enthusiasm for patriotism and its widespread reputation. We have specially sent a sample of the silk for your reference and hope that you will vigorously promote its use in order to expand sales and save our rights and interests. We remain in hopeful anticipation. Sincerely, the Lake Society Committee.
